1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# big-code-k8s-arch-001: Kubernetes Scheduler Architecture

## Task

Explain the Kubernetes scheduler architecture and how a Pod gets assigned to a Node. Trace the complete scheduling pipeline from when a Pod enters the scheduling queue to when it is bound to a Node, including the plugin framework, extension points, and the two-phase (scheduling cycle + binding cycle) design.

## Context

- **Repository**: github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.30.0 (mirror of github.com/sg-evals)/kubernetes--v1.30.0 (mirror of kubernetes/kubernetes) (Go, ~2.5M LOC)
- **Category**: Architectural Understanding
- **Difficulty**: hard
- **Subsystem Focus**: pkg/scheduler/ — the kube-scheduler component

## Requirements

1. Identify all files involved in the scheduler subsystem (scheduler core, framework, queue, cache, plugins)
2. Trace the dependency chain from the main scheduling loop through the scheduling cycle and binding cycle
3. Document the plugin framework architecture (extension points: PreFilter, Filter, Score, Reserve, Permit, Bind)
4. Explain how the SchedulingQueue, Cache, and CycleState interact during a scheduling cycle

## Expected Output

Write your analysis to `/logs/agent/solution.md` with the following structure:

```
## Files Examined
- path/to/file1.ext — role in architecture
- path/to/file2.ext — role in architecture
...

## Dependency Chain
1. Entry point: path/to/entry.ext
2. Calls: path/to/next.ext (via function/method name)
3. Delegates to: path/to/impl.ext
...

## Analysis
[Detailed architectural analysis including:
- Design patterns identified
- Component responsibilities
- Data flow description
- Interface contracts between components]

## Summary
[Concise 2-3 sentence summary answering the task question]
```

## Evaluation Criteria

- File recall: Did you find the correct set of architecturally relevant files?
- Dependency accuracy: Did you trace the correct dependency/call chain?
- Architectural coherence: Did you correctly identify the design patterns and component relationships?

44-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive analysis of the Kubernetes scheduler architecture. Here's what I've documented:

## Key Findings

**Architecture Overview:**
- The scheduler implements a **two-phase lock-free design**: 
  1. **Scheduling Cycle** (sync): Pod flows through filter/score plugins synchronously, gets assumed in cache
  2. **Binding Cycle** (async): Binding happens in separate goroutine, doesn't block scheduler

**12 Extension Points:**
PreEnqueue → QueueSort → PreFilter → Filter → PostFilter → PreScore → Score → Reserve → Permit → PreBind → Bind → PostBind

**Core Components:**
1. **SchedulingQueue** - Three-tier queue (activeQ, backoffQ, unschedulablePods) with queueing hints for efficient requeuing
2. **Cache** - Maintains "assumed" pods (pessimistic locking), generates snapshots at cycle start
3. **CycleState** - Thread-safe sync.Map for sharing state between plugins within a cycle
4. **Framework** - Plugin registry and executor; instantiates plugins and runs them at extension points
5. **Profiles** - Multiple scheduler configurations can run simultaneously

**Data Flow:**
Pod enters queue → ScheduleOne pops it → Plugins filter/score nodes → Best node selected → Pod assumed in cache → Reserve/Permit plugins verify → Binding runs async → PreBind/Bind/PostBind execute → Done

The analysis has been written to `/logs/agent/solution.md` with detailed dependency chains, architectural patterns, data structures, and the complete scheduling pipeline.

}\n371: \n372: func buildQueueingHintMap(es []framework.EnqueueExtensions) internalqueue.QueueingHintMap {\n373: \tqueueingHintMap := make(internalqueue.QueueingHintMap)\n374: \tfor _, e := range es {\n375: \t\tevents := e.EventsToRegister()\n376: \n377: \t\t// This will happen when plugin registers with empty events, it's usually the case a pod\n378: \t\t// will become reschedulable only for self-update, e.g. schedulingGates plugin, the pod\n379: \t\t// will enter into the activeQ via priorityQueue.Update().\n380: \t\tif len(events) == 0 {\n381: \t\t\tcontinue\n382: \t\t}\n383: \n384: \t\t// Note: Rarely, a plugin implements EnqueueExtensions but returns nil.\n385: \t\t// We treat it as: the plugin is not interested in any event, and hence pod failed by that plugin\n386: \t\t// cannot be moved by any regular cluster event.\n387: \t\t// So, we can just ignore such EventsToRegister here.\n388: \n389: \t\tregisterNodeAdded := false\n390: \t\tregisterNodeTaintUpdated := false\n391: \t\tfor _, event := range events {\n392: \t\t\tfn := event.QueueingHintFn\n393: \t\t\tif fn == nil || !utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.SchedulerQueueingHints) {\n394: \t\t\t\tfn = defaultQueueingHintFn\n395: \t\t\t}\n396: \n397: \t\t\tif event.Event.Resource == framework.Node {\n398: \t\t\t\tif event.Event.ActionType&framework.Add != 0 {\n399: \t\t\t\t\tregisterNodeAdded = true\n400: \t\t\t\t}\n401: \t\t\t\tif event.Event.ActionType&framework.UpdateNodeTaint != 0 {\n402: \t\t\t\t\tregisterNodeTaintUpdated = true\n403: \t\t\t\t}\n404: \t\t\t}\n405: \n406: \t\t\tqueueingHintMap[event.Event] = append(queueingHintMap[event.Event], &internalqueue.QueueingHintFunction{\n407: \t\t\t\tPluginName:     e.Name(),\n408: \t\t\t\tQueueingHintFn: fn,\n409: \t\t\t})\n410: \t\t}\n411: \t\tif registerNodeAdded && !registerNodeTaintUpdated {\n412: \t\t\t// Temporally fix for the issue https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/109437\n413: \t\t\t// NodeAdded QueueingHint isn't always called because of preCheck.\n414: \t\t\t// It's definitely not something expected for plugin developers,\n415: \t\t\t// and registering UpdateNodeTaint event is the only mitigation for now.\n416: \t\t\t//\n417: \t\t\t// So, here registers UpdateNodeTaint event for plugins that has NodeAdded event, but don't have UpdateNodeTaint event.\n418: \t\t\t// It has a bad impact for the requeuing efficiency though, a lot better than some Pods being stuch in the\n419: \t\t\t// unschedulable pod pool.\n420: \t\t\t// This behavior will be removed when we remove the preCheck feature.\n421: \t\t\t// See: https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/110175\n422: \t\t\tqueueingHintMap[framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.Node, ActionType: framework.UpdateNodeTaint}] =\n423: \t\t\t\tappend(queueingHintMap[framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.Node, ActionType: framework.UpdateNodeTaint}],\n424: \t\t\t\t\t&internalqueue.QueueingHintFunction{\n425: \t\t\t\t\t\tPluginName:     e.Name(),\n426: \t\t\t\t\t\tQueueingHintFn: defaultQueueingHintFn,\n427: \t\t\t\t\t},\n428: \t\t\t\t)\n429: \t\t}\n430: \t}\n431: \treturn queueingHintMap\n432: }\n433: \n434: // Run begins watching and scheduling. It starts scheduling and blocked until the context is done.\n435: func (sched *Scheduler) Run(ctx context.Context) {\n436: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n437: \tsched.SchedulingQueue.Run(logger)\n438: \n439: \t// We need to start scheduleOne loop in a dedicated goroutine,\n440: \t// because scheduleOne function hangs on getting the next item\n441: \t// from the SchedulingQueue.\n442: \t// If there are no new pods to schedule, it will be hanging there\n443: \t// and if done in this goroutine it will be blocking closing\n444: \t// SchedulingQueue, in satisfy the io.Closer interface, they are closed.\n451: \terr := sched.Profiles.Close()\n452: \tif err != nil {\n453: \t\tlogger.Error(err, \"Failed to close plugins\")\n454: \t}\n455: }\n456: \n457: \treturn informerFactory\n463: }\n464: \n465: func buildExtenders(logger klog.Logger, extenders []schedulerapi.Extender, profiles []schedulerapi.KubeSchedulerProfile) ([]framework.Extender, error) {\n466: \tvar fExtenders []framework.Extender\n467: \tif len(extenders) == 0 {\n468: \t\treturn nil, nil\n469: \t}\n470: \n471: \tvar ignoredExtendedResources []string\n472: \tvar ignorableExtenders have an effect on ComponentConfig, where it is possible to configure Extenders and\n495: \t// plugin args (and in which case the extender ignored resources take precedence).\n496: \tif \\n859: // selectHost takes a prioritized list of nodes and then picks one\\n860: // in a reservoir sampling manner from the nodes that had the highest score.\\n861: // It also returns the top {count} Nodes,\\n862: // and the top of the list will be always the selected host.\\n863: func selectHost(nodeScoreList []framework.NodePluginScores, count int) (string, []framework.NodePluginScores, error) {\\n864: \\tif len(nodeScoreList) == 0 {\\n865: \\t\\treturn \\\"\\\", nil, errEmptyPriorityList\\n866: \\t}\\n867: \\n868: \\tvar h nodeScoreHeap = nodeScoreList\\n869: \\theap.Init(&h)\\n870: \\tcntOfMaxScore := 1\\n871: \\tselectedIndex := 0\\n872: \\t// The top of the heap is the NodeScoreResult with the highest score.\\n873: \\tsortedNodeScoreList := make([]framework.NodePluginScores, 0, count)\\n874: \\tsortedNodeScoreList = append(sortedNodeScoreList, heap.Pop(&h).(framework.NodePluginScores))\\n875: \\n876: \\t// This for-loop will continue until all Nodes with the highest scores get checked for a reservoir sampling,\\n877: \\t// and sortedNodeScoreList gets (count - 1) elements.\\n878: \\tfor ns := heap.Pop(&h).(framework.NodePluginScores); ; ns = heap.Pop(&h).(framework.NodePluginScores) {\\n879: \\t\\tif ns.TotalScore != sortedNodeScoreList[0].TotalScore && len(sortedNodeScoreList) == count {\\n880: \\t\\t\\tbreak\\n881: \\t\\t}\\n882: \\n883: \\t\\tif ns.TotalScore == sortedNodeScoreList[0].TotalScore {\\n884: \\t\\t\\tcntOfMaxScore++\\n885: \\t\\t\\tif rand.Intn(cntOfMaxScore) == 0 {\\n886: \\t\\t\\t\\t// Replace the candidate with probability of 1/cntOfMaxScore\\n887: \\t\\t\\t\\tselectedIndex = cntOfMaxScore - 1\\n888: \\t\\t\\t}\\n889: \\t\\t}\\n890: \\n891: \\t\\tsortedNodeScoreList = append(sortedNodeScoreList, n-1]\\n931: \\treturn x\\n932: }\\n933: \\n934: // assume signals to the cache that a pod is already in the cache, so that binding can be asynchronous.\\n935: // assume modifies `assumed`.\\n936: func framework.NewStatus(framework.Unschedulable).WithError(err)\n190: \t}\n191: \n192: \tmetrics.SchedulingAlgorithmLatency.Observe(metrics.SinceInSeconds(start))\n193: \t// Tell the cache to assume that podInfo.DeepCopy()\n196: \tassumedPod := assumedPodInfo.Pod\n197: \t// assume modifies `assumedPod` by setting NodeName=scheduleResult.SuggestedHost\n198: \terr = sched.assume(logger, assumedPod, scheduleResult.SuggestedHost)\n199: \tif err != nil {\n200: \t\t// This is most probably result of a BUG in retrying logic.\n201: \t\t// We report an error here so that pod scheduling can be retried.\n202: \t\t// This relies on the fact that Error will check if the pod has been bound\n203: \t\t// to a node and if so will not add it back to the unscheduled pods queue\n204: \t\t// (otherwise this would cause an infinite loop).\n205: \t\treturn ScheduleResult{nominatingInfo: clearNominatedNode}, assumedPodInfo, framework.AsStatus(err)\n206: \t}\n207: \n208: \t// Run the Reserve method of reserve plugins.\n209: \tif sts := fwk.RunReservePluginsReserve(ctx, state, assumedPod, scheduleResult.SuggestedHost); !sts.IsSuccess() {\n210: \t\t// trigger un-reserve to clean up state associated with the reserved Pod\n211: \t\tfwk.RunReservePluginsUnreserve(ctx, state, assumedPod, scheduleResult.SuggestedHost)\n212: \t\tif forgetErr := sched.Cache.ForgetPod(logger, assumedPod); forgetErr != nil {\n213: \t\t\tlogger.Error(forgetErr, \"Scheduler cache ForgetPod failed\")\n214: \t\t}\n215: \n216: \t\tif sts.IsRejected() {\n217: \t\t\tfitErr := &framework.FitError{\n218: \t\t\t\tNumAllNodes: 1,\n219: \t\t\t\tPod:         pod,\n220: \t\t\t\tDiagnosis: framework.Diagnosis{\n221: \t\t\t\t\tNodeToStatusMap: framework.NodeToStatusMap{scheduleResult.SuggestedHost: sts},\n222: \t\t\t\t},\n223: \t\t\t}\n224: \t\t\tfitErr.Diagnosis.AddPluginStatus(sts)\n225: \t\t\treturn ScheduleResult{nominatingInfo: clearNominatedNode}, assumedPodInfo, framework.NewStatus(sts.Code()).WithError(fitErr)\n226: \t\t}\n227: \t\treturn ScheduleResult{nominatingInfo: clearNominatedNode}, assumedPodInfo, sts\n228: \t}\n229: \n230: \t// Run \"permit\" plugins.\n231: \trunPermitStatus := fwk.RunPermitPlugins(ctx, state, assumedPod, scheduleResult.SuggestedHost)\n232: \tif !runPermitStatus.IsWait() && !runPermitStatus.IsSuccess() {\n233: \t\t// trigger un-reserve to clean up state associated with the reserved Pod\n234: \t\tfwk.RunReservePluginsUnreserve(ctx, state, assumedPod, scheduleResult.SuggestedHost)\n235: \t\tif forgetErr := sched.Cache.ForgetPod(logger, assumedPod); forgetErr != nil {\n236: \t\t\tlogger.Error(forgetErr, \"Scheduler cache ForgetPod failed\")\n237: \t\t}\n238: \n239: \t\tif runPermitStatus.IsRejected() {\n240: \t\t\tfitErr := &framework.FitError{\n241: \t\t\t\tNumAllNodes: 1,\n242: \t\t\t\tPod:         pod,\n243: \t\t\t\tDiagnosis: framework.Diagnosis{\n244: \t\t\t\t\tNodeToStatusMap: framework.NodeToStatusMap{scheduleResult.SuggestedHost: runPermitStatus},\n245: \t\t\t\t},\n246: \t\t\t}\n247: \t\t\tfitErr.Diagnosis.AddPluginStatus(runPermitStatus)\n248: \t\t\treturn ScheduleResult{nominatingInfo: clearNominatedNode}, assumedPodInfo, framework.NewStatus(runPermitStatus.Code()).WithError(fitErr)\n249: \t\t}\n250: \n251: \t\treturn ScheduleResult{nominatingInfo: clearNominatedNode}, assumedPodInfo, runPermitStatus\n252: \t}\n253: \n254: \t// At the end of a successful scheduling cycle, pop and move up Pods if needed.\n255: \tif len(podsToActivate.Map) != 0 {\n256: \t\tsched.SchedulingQueue.Activate(logger, podsToActivate.Map)\n257: \t\t// Clear the entries after activation.\n258: \t\tpodsToActivate.Map = make(map[string]*v1.Pod)\n259: \t}\n260: \n261: \treturn scheduleResult, assumedPodInfo, nil\n262: }\n263: \n264: // bindingCycle tries to bind an assumed Pod.\n265: func (sched *Scheduler) bindingCycle(\n266: \tctx context.Context,\n267: \tstate *framework.CycleState,\n268: \tfwk framework.Framework,\n269: \tscheduleResult ScheduleResult,\n270: \tassumedPodInfo *framework.QueuedPodInfo,\n271: \tstart time.Time,\n272: \tpodsToActivate *framework.PodsToActivate) *framework.Status {\n273: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n274: \n275: \tassumedPod := assumedPodInfo.Pod\n276: \n277: \t// Run \"permit\" plugins.\n278: \tif status := fwk.WaitOnPermit(ctx, assumedPod); !status.IsSuccess() {\n279: \t\tif status.IsRejected() {\n280: \t\t\tfitErr := &framework.FitError{\n281: \t\t\t\tNumAllNodes: 1,\n282: \t\t\t\tPod:         assumedPodInfo.Pod,\n283: \t\t\t\tDiagnosis: framework.Diagnosis{\n284: \t\t\t\t\tNodeToStatusMap:      framework.NodeToStatusMap{scheduleResult.SuggestedHost: status},\n285: \t\t\t\t\tUnschedulablePlugins: sets.New(status.Plugin()),\n286: \t\t\t\t},\n287: \t\t\t}\n288: \t\t\treturn framework.NewStatus(status.Code()).WithError(fitErr)\n289: \t\t}\n290: \t\treturn \t}\n302: \n303: \t// Calculating nodeResourceString can be heavy. Avoid it if klog verbosity is below 2.\n304: \tlogger.V(2).Info(\"Successfully bound pod to node\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(assumedPod), \"node\", scheduleResult.SuggestedHost, \"evaluatedNodes\", scheduleResult.EvaluatedNodes, \"feasibleNodes\", scheduleResult.FeasibleNodes)\n305: \tmetrics.PodScheduled(fwk.ProfileName(), metrics.SinceInSeconds(start))\n306: \tmetrics.PodSchedulingAttempts.Observe(float64(assumedPodInfo.Attempts))\n307: \tif assumedPodInfo.InitialAttemptTimestamp != nil {\n308: \t\tmetrics.PodSchedulingDuration.WithLabelValues(getAttemptsLabel(assumedPodInfo)).Observe(metrics.SinceInSeconds(*assumedPodInfo.InitialAttemptTimestamp))\n309: \t\tmetrics.PodSchedulingSLIDuration.WithLabelValues(getAttemptsLabel(assumedPodInfo)).Observe(metrics.SinceInSeconds(*assumedPodInfo.InitialAttemptTimestamp))\n310: \t}\n311: \t// Run \"postbind\" plugins.\n312: \tfwk.RunPostBindPlugins(ctx, state, assumedPod, scheduleResult.SuggestedHost)\n313: \n314: \t// At the end of a successful binding cycle, move up Pods if needed.\n315: \tif len(podsToActivate.Map) != 0 {\n316: \t\tsched.SchedulingQueue.Activate(logger, podsToActivate.Map)\n317: \t\t// Unlike the logic in schedulingCycle(), we don't bother deleting the entries\n318: \t\t// as `podsToActivate.Map` is no longer consumed.\n319: \t}\n320: \n321: \treturn nil\n322: }\n323: \n324: func (sched *Scheduler) handleBindingCycleError(\n325: \tctx context.Context,\n326: \tstate *framework.CycleState,\n327: \tfwk framework.Framework,\n328: \tpodInfo *framework.QueuedPodInfo,\n329: \tstart time.Time,\n330: \tscheduleResult ScheduleResult,\n331: \tstatus *framework.Status) {\n332: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n333: \n334: \tassumedPod := podInfo.Pod\n335: \t// trigger un-reserve plugins to clean up state associated with the reserved Pod\n336: \tfwk.RunReservePluginsUnreserve(ctx, state, assumedPod, scheduleResult.SuggestedHost)\n337: \tif forgetErr := sched.Cache.ForgetPod(logger, assumedPod); forgetErr != nil {\n338: \t\tlogger.Error(forgetErr, \"scheduler cache ForgetPod failed\")\n339: \t} else {\n340: \t\t// \"Forget\"ing an assumed Pod in binding cycle should be treated as a PodDelete event,\n341: \t\t// as the assumed Pod had occupied a certain amount of resources in scheduler cache.\n342: \t\t//\n343: \t\t// Avoid moving the assumed Pod itself as it's always Unschedulable.\n344: \t\t// It's intentional to \"defer\" this operation; otherwise MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue() would\n345: \t\t// add this event to in-flight events and thus move the assumed pod to backoffQ anyways if the plugins don't have appropriate QueueingHint.\n346: \t\tif status.IsRejected() {\n347: \t\t\tdefer sched.SchedulingQueue.MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue(logger, internalqueue.AssignedPodDelete, assumedPod, nil, func(pod *v1.Pod) bool {\n348: \t\t\t\treturn assumedPod.UID != pod.UID\n349: \t\t\t})\n350: \t\t} else {\n351: \t\t\tsched.SchedulingQueue.MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue(logger, internalqueue.AssignedPodDelete, assumedPod, nil, nil)\n352: \t\t}\n353: \t}\n354: \n355: \tsched.FailureHandler(ctx, fwk, podInfo, status, clearNominatedNode, start)\n356: }\n357: \n358: func (sched *Scheduler) frameworkForPod(pod *v1.Pod) (framework.Framework, error) {\n359: \tfwk, ok := sched.Profiles[pod.Spec.SchedulerName]\n360: \tif !ok {\n361: \t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"profile not found for scheduler name %q\", pod.Spec.SchedulerName)\n362: \t}\n363: \treturn fwk, nil\n364: }\n365: \n366: // skipPodSchedule returns true if we could skip scheduling the pod for specified cases.\n367: func (sched *Scheduler) skipPodSchedule(ctx context.Context, fwk framework.Framework, pod *v1.Pod) bool {\n368: \t// Case 1: pod is being deleted.\n369: \tif pod.DeletionTimestamp != nil {\n370: \t\tfwk.EventRecorder().Eventf(pod, nil, v1.EventTypeWarning, \"FailedScheduling\", \"Scheduling\", \"skip schedule deleting pod: %v/%v\", pod.Namespace, pod.Name)\n371: node list.\n388: // If it succeeds, it will return the name of the node.\n389: // If it fails, it will return a FitError with reasons.\n390: func (sched *Scheduler) schedulePod(ctx context.Context, fwk framework.Framework, state *framework.CycleState, pod *v1.Pod) (result ScheduleResult, err error) {\n391: \ttrace := utiltrace.New(\"Scheduling\", utiltrace.Field{Key: \"namespace\", Value: pod.Namespace}, utiltrace.Field{Key: \"name\", Value: pod.Name})\n392: \tdefer trace.LogIfLong(100 * time.Millisecond)\n393: \tif err := sched.Cache.UpdateSnapshot(klog.FromContext(ctx), sched.nodeInfoSnapshot); err != nil {\n394: \t\treturn result, err\n395: \t}\n396: \ttrace.Step(\"Snapshotting scheduler cache and node infos done\")\n397: \n398: \tif sched.nodeInfoSnapshot.NumNodes() == 0 {\n399: \t\treturn result, ErrNoNodesAvailable\n400: \t}\n401: \n402: \tfeasibleNodes, diagnosis, err := sched.findNodesThatFitPod(ctx, fwk, state, pod)\n403: \tif err != nil {\n404: \t\treturn result, err\n405: \t}\n406: \ttrace.Step(\"Computing predicates done\")\n407: \n408: \tif len(feasibleNodes) == 0 {\n409: \t\treturn result, &framework.FitError{\n410: \t\t\tPod:         pod,\n411: \t\t\tNumAllNodes: sched.nodeInfoSnapshot.NumNodes(),\n412: \t\t\tDiagnosis:   diagnosis,\n413: \t\t}\n414: \t}\n415: \n416: \t// When only one \t\tFeasibleNodes:  len(feasibleNodes),\n437: \t}, err\n438: }\n439: \n440: // Filters the nodes to find the ones that fit the pod based on the framework\n441: // filter plugins and filter extenders.\n442: func (sched *Scheduler) findNodesThatFitPod(ctx context.Context, fwk framework.Framework, state *framework.CycleState, pod *v1.Pod) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, framework.Diagnosis, error) {\n443: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n444: \tdiagnosis := framework.Diagnosis{\n445: \t\tNodeToStatusMap: make(framework.NodeToStatusMap),\n446: \t}\n447: \n448: \tallNodes, err := sched.nodeInfoSnapshot.NodeInfos().List()\n449: \tif err != nil {\n450: \t\treturn nil, diagnosis, err\n451: \t}\n452: \t// Run \"prefilter\" plugins.\n453: \tpreRes, s := fwk.RunPreFilterPlugins(ctx, state, pod)\n454: \tif !s.IsSuccess() {\n455: \t\tif !s.IsRejected() {\n456: \t\t\treturn nil, diagnosis, s.AsError()\n457: \t\t}\n458: \t\t// All nodes in NodeToStatusMap will have the same status so that they can be handled in the preemption.\n459: \t\t// Some non trivial refactoring is needed to avoid this copy.\n460: \t\tfor _, n := range allNodes {\n461: \t\t\tdiagnosis.NodeToStatusMap[n.Node().Name] = s\n462: \t\t}\n463: \n464: \t\t// Record the messages from PreFilter in Diagnosis.PreFilterMsg.\n465: \t\tmsg := s.Message()\n466: \t\tdiagnosis.PreFilterMsg = msg\n467: \t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"Status after running PreFilter plugins for pod\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"status\", msg)\n468: \t\tdiagnosis.AddPluginStatus(s)\n469: \t\treturn nil, diagnosis, nil\n470: \t}\n471: \n472: \t// \"NominatedNodeName\" can potentially be set in a previous scheduling cycle as a result of preemption.\n473: \t// This node is likely the only candidate that will fit the pod, and hence we try it first before iterating over all nodes.\n474: \tif len(pod.Status.NominatedNodeName) > 0 {\n475: \t\tfeasibleNodes, err := sched.evaluateNominatedNode(ctx, pod, fwk, state, diagnosis)\n476: \t\tif err != nil {\n477: \t\t\tlogger.Error(err, \"Evaluation failed on nominated node\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"node\", pod.Status.NominatedNodeName)\n478: \t\t}\n479: \t\t// Nominated node passes all the filters, scheduler is good to assign this node to the pod.\n480: \t\tif len(feasibleNodes) != 0 {\n481: \t\t\treturn feasibleNodes, diagnosis, nil\n482: \t\t}\n483: \t}\n484: \n485: \tnodes := allNodes\n486: \tif !preRes.AllNodes() {\n487: \t\tnodes = make([]*framework.NodeInfo, 0, len(preRes.NodeNames))\n488: \t\tfor _, n := range allNodes {\n489: \t\t\tif !preRes.NodeNames.Has(n.Node().Name) {\n490: \t\t\t\t// We consider Nodes that are filtered out by PreFilterResult as rejected via UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n491: \t\t\t\t// We have to record them in NodeToStatusMap so that they won't be considered as candidates in the preemption.\n492: \t\t\t\tdiagnosis.NodeToStatusMap[n.Node().Name] = framework.NewStatus(framework.UnschedulableAndUnresolvable, \"node is filtered out by the prefilter result\")\n493: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n494: \t\t\t}\n495: \t\t\tnodes = append(nodes, n)\n496: \t\t}\n497: \t}\n498: \tfeasibleNodes, err := sched.findNodesThatPassFilters(ctx, fwk, state, pod, &diagnosis, nodes)\n499: \t// always try to update the sched.nextStartNodeIndex regardless of whether an error has occurred\n500: \t// this is helpful to make sure that all the nodes have a chance to be searched\n501: \tprocessedNodes := len(feasibleNodes) + len(diagnosis.NodeToStatusMap)\n502: \tsched.nextStartNodeIndex = (sched.nextStartNodeIndex + processedNodes) % len(nodes)\n503: \tif err != nil {\n504: \t\treturn nil, diagnosis, err\n505: \t}\n506: \n507: \tfeasibleNodesAfterExtender, err := findNodesThatPassExtenders(ctx, sched.Extenders, pod, feasibleNodes, diagnosis.NodeToStatusMap)\n508: \tif err != nil {\n509: \t\treturn nil, diagnosis, err\n510: \t}\n511: \tif len(feasibleNodesAfterExtender) != len(feasibleNodes) {\n512: \t\t// Extenders filtered out some nodes.\n513: \t\t//\n514: \t\t// Extender doesn't support any kind of requeueing feature like EnqueueExtensions in the scheduling framework.\n515: \t\t// When Extenders reject some Nodes and the pod ends up being unschedulable,\n516: \t\t// we put framework.ExtenderName to pInfo.UnschedulablePlugins.\n517: \t\t// This Pod will be requeued from unschedulable pod pool to activeQ/backoffQ\n518: \t\t// by any kind of cluster events.\n519: \t\t// https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/122019\n520: \t\tif diagnosis.UnschedulablePlugins == nil {\n521: \t\t\tdiagnosis.UnschedulablePlugins = sets.New[string]()\n522: \t\t}\n523: \t\tdiagnosis.UnschedulablePlugins.Insert(framework.ExtenderName)\n524: \t}\n525: \n526: \treturn feasibleNodesAfterExtender, diagnosis, nil\n527: }\n528: \n529: func (sched *Scheduler) evaluateNominatedNode(ctx context.Context, pod *v1.Pod, fwk framework.Framework, state *framework.CycleState, diagnosis framework.Diagnosis) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, error) {\n530: \tnnn := nil\n547: }\n548: \n549: // hasScoring checks if scoring nodes is configured.\n550: func (sched *Scheduler) hasScoring(fwk framework.Framework) bool {\n551: \tif fwk.HasScorePlugins() {\n552: \n562: // hasExtenderFilters checks if any extenders filter nodes.\n563: func (sched *Scheduler) hasExtenderFilters() bool {\n564: \tfor _, extender := range sched.Extenders {\n565: \t\tif *Scheduler) findNodesThatPassFilters(\n574: \tctx context.Context,\n575: \tfwk framework.Framework,\n576: \tstate *framework.CycleState,\n577: \tpod *v1.Pod,\n578: \tdiagnosis *framework.Diagnosis,\n579: \tnodes []*framework.NodeInfo) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, error) {\n580: \tnumAllNodes := len(nodes)\n581: \tnumNodesToFind := sched.numFeasibleNodesToFind(fwk.PercentageOfNodesToScore(), int32(numAllNodes))\n582: \tif !sched.hasExtenderFilters() && !sched.hasScoring(fwk) {\n583: \t\tnumNodesToFind = 1\n584: \t}\n585: \n586: \t// Create feasible list with enough space to avoid growing it\n587: \t// and allow assigning.\n588: \tfeasibleNodes := make([]*framework.NodeInfo, numNodesToFind)\n589: \n590: \tif !fwk.HasFilterPlugins() {\n591: \t\tfor i := range feasibleNodes {\n592: \t\t\tfeasibleNodes[i] = nodes[(sched.nextStartNodeIndex+i)%numAllNodes]\n593: \t\t}\n594: \t\treturn feasibleNodes, nil\n595: \t}\n596: \n597: \terrCh := parallelize.NewErrorChannel()\n598: \tvar feasibleNodesLen int32\n599: \tctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(ctx)\n600: \tdefer cancel()\n601: \n602: \ttype nodeStatus struct {\n603: \t\tnode   string\n604: \t\tstatus *framework.Status\n605: \t}\n606: \tresult := make([]*nodeStatus, numAllNodes)\n607: \tcheckNode := func(i int) {\n608: \t\t// We check the nodes starting from where we left off in the previous scheduling cycle,\n609: \t\t// this is to make sure all nodes have the same chance of being examined across pods.\n610: \t\tnodeInfo := \t\t\terrCh.SendErrorWithCancel(status.AsError(), cancel)\n614: \t\t\treturn\n615: \t\t}\n616: \t\tif status.IsSuccess() {\n617: \t\t\tlength := atomic.AddInt32(&feasibleNodesLen, 1)\n618: \t\t\tif length > numNodesToFind {\n619: \t\t\t\tcancel()\n620: \t\t\t\tatomic.AddInt32(&feasibleNodesLen, -1)\n621: \t\t\t} else {\n622: \t\t\t\tfeasibleNodes[length-1] = nodeInfo\n623: \t\t\t}\n624: \t\t} else {\n625: \t\t\tresult[i] = &nodeStatus{node: nodeInfo.Node().Name, status: status}\n626: \t\t}\n627: \t}\n628: \n629: \tbeginCheckNode := time.Now()\n630: \tstatusCode := framework.Success\n631: \tdefer func() {\n632: \t\t// We record Filter extension point latency here instead of in framework.go because framework.RunFilterPlugins\n633: \t\t// function is called for each node, whereas we want to have an overall latency for all nodes per scheduling cycle.\n634: \t\t// Note that this latency also includes latency for `addNominatedPods`, which calls framework.RunPreFilterAddPod.\n635: \t\tmetrics.FrameworkExtensionPointDuration.WithLabelValues(metrics.Filter, statusCode.String(), fwk.ProfileName()).Observe(metrics.SinceInSeconds(beginCheckNode))\n636: \t}()\n637: \n638: \t// Stops searching for more nodes once the configured number of feasible nodes\n639: \t// are found.\n640: \tfwk.Parallelizer().Until(ctx, numAllNodes, checkNode, metrics.Filter)\n641: \tfeasibleNodes = feasibleNodes[:feasibleNodesLen]\n642: \tfor _, item := range result {\n643: \t\tif item == nil {\n644: \t\t\tcontinue\n645: \t\t}\n646: \t\tdiagnosis.NodeToStatusMap[item.node] = item.status\n647: \t\tdiagnosis.AddPluginStatus(item.status)\n648: \t}\n649: \tif err := errCh.ReceiveError(); err != nil {\n650: \t\tstatusCode = framework.Error\n651: \t\treturn feasibleNodes, err\n652: \t}\n653: \treturn feasibleNodes, nil\n654: }\n655: \n656: // numFeasibleNodesToFind returns the number of feasible nodes that once found, the scheduler stops\n657: // its search for more feasible nodes.\n658: func (sched *Scheduler) numFeasibleNodesToFind(percentageOfNodesToScore *int32, numAllNodes int32) (numNodes int32) {\n659: \tif numAllNodes < minFeasibleNodesToFind {\n660: \t\treturn numAllNodes\n661: \t}\n662: \n663: \t// Use profile percentageOfNodesToScore if it's set. Otherwise, use global percentageOfNodesToScore.\n664: \tvar percentage int32\n665: \tif percentageOfNodesToScore != nil {\n666: \t\tpercentage = *percentageOfNodesToScore\n667: \t} else {\n668: \t\t\t}\n733: \t\t}\n734: \n735: \t\tfeasibleNodes = feasibleList\n736: \t}\n737: \treturn feasibleNodes, nil\n738: }\n739: \n740: // prioritizeNodes prioritizes the nodes by running the score extenders are run as well.\n744: // All scores are finally combined (added) to get the total weighted scores of all nodes\n745: func prioritizeNodes(\n746: \tctx context.Context,\n747: \textenders Only one queue sort\n350: // plugin may be enabled at a time.\n351: type QueueSortPlugin interface {\n352: \tPlugin\n353: \t// Less are used to sort pods in the scheduling queue.\n354: \tLess(*QueuedPodInfo, *QueuedPodInfo) bool\n355: }\n356: \n357: // EnqueueExtensions is an optional interface that plugins can implement to efficiently\n358: // move unschedulable Pods in internal scheduling queues.\n359: // In the scheduler, Pods can be unschedulable by PreEnqueue, PreFilter, Filter, Reserve, and Permit plugins,\n360: // and Pods rejected by these plugins are requeued based on this extension point.\n361: // Failures from other extension points are regarded as temporal errors (e.g., network failure),\n362: // and the scheduler requeue Pods without this extension point - always requeue Pods to activeQ after backoff.\n363: // This is because such temporal errors cannot be resolved by specific cluster events,\n364: // and we have no choise but keep retrying scheduling until the failure is resolved.\n365: //\n366: // Plugins that make pod unschedulable (PreEnqueue, PreFilter, Filter, Reserve, and Permit plugins) should implement this interface,\n367: // otherwise the default implementation will be used, which is less efficient in requeueing Pods rejected by the plugin.\n368: // And, if plugins other than above extension points support this interface, they are just ignored.\n369: type EnqueueExtensions interface {\n370: \tPlugin\n371: \t// EventsToRegister returns a series of possible events that may cause a Pod\n372: \t// failed by this plugin schedulable. Each event has a callback function that\n373: \t// filters out events to reduce useless retry of Pod's scheduling.\n374: \t// The events will be registered when instantiating the internal scheduling queue,\n375: \t// and leveraged to build event handlers dynamically.\n376: \t// Note: the returned list needs to be static (not depend on configuration parameters);\n377: \t// otherwise it would lead to undefined behavior.\n378: \t//\n379: \t// Appropriate implementation of this function will make Pod's re-scheduling accurate and performant.\n380: \tEventsToRegister() []ClusterEventWithHint\n381: }\n382: \n383: // PreFilterExtensions is an interface that is included in plugins that allow specifying\n384: // callbacks to make incremental updates to its supposedly pre-calculated\n385: // state.\n386: type PreFilterExtensions interface {\n387: \t// AddPod is called by the framework while trying to evaluate the impact\n388: \t// of adding podToAdd to the node while scheduling podToSchedule.\n389: \tAddPod(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, podToSchedule *v1.Pod, podInfoToAdd *PodInfo, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\n390: \t// RemovePod is called by the framework while trying to evaluate the impact\n391: \t// of removing podToRemove from the node while scheduling podToSchedule.\n392: \tRemovePod(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, podToSchedule *v1.Pod, podInfoToRemove *PodInfo, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\n393: }\n394: \n395: // PreFilterPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"PreFilter\" plugins.\n396: // These plugins are called at the beginning of the scheduling cycle.\n397: type PreFilterPlugin interface {\n398: \tPlugin\n399: \t// PreFilter is called at the beginning of the scheduling cycle. All PreFilter\n400: \t// plugins must return success or the pod will be rejected. PreFilter could optionally\n401: \t// return a PreFilterResult to influence which nodes to evaluate downstream. This is useful\n402: \t// for cases where it is possible to determine the subset of nodes to process in O(1) time.\n403: \t// When PreFilterResult filters out some Nodes, the framework considers Nodes that are filtered out as getting \"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\".\n404: \t// i.e., those Nodes will be out of the candidates of the preemption.\n405: \t//\n406: \t// When it returns Skip status, returned PreFilterResult and other fields in status are just ignored,\n407: \t// and coupled Filter plugin/PreFilterExtensions() will be skipped in this scheduling cycle.\n408: \tPreFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod) (*PreFilterResult, *Status)\n409: \t// PreFilterExtensions returns a PreFilterExtensions interface if the plugin implements one,\n410: \t// or nil if it does not. The framework guarantees that the extensions\n412: \t// AddPod/RemovePod will only be called after PreFilter, possibly on a cloned\n413: \t// CycleState, and may call those functions more than once before calling\n414: \t// Filter again on a specific node.\n415: \tPreFilterExtensions() PreFilterExtensions\n416: }\n417: \n418: // FilterPlugin is an interface for Filter plugins. These plugins are called at the\n419: // filter extension point for filtering out hosts that cannot run a pod.\n420: // This concept used to be called 'predicate' in the original scheduler.\n421: // These plugins should return \"Success\", \"Unschedulable\" or \"Error\" in Status.code.\n422: // However, the scheduler accepts other valid codes as well.\n423: // Anything other than \"Success\" will lead to exclusion of the given host from\n424: // running the pod.\n425: type FilterPlugin interface {\n426: \tPlugin\n427: \t// Filter is called by the scheduling framework.\n428: \t// All FilterPlugins should return \"Success\" to declare that\n429: \t// the given node fits the pod. If Filter doesn't return \"Success\",\n430: \t// it will return \"Unschedulable\", \"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\" or \"Error\".\n431: \t// For the node being evaluated, Filter plugins should look at the passed\n432: \t// nodeInfo reference for this particular node's information (e.g., pods\n433: \t// considered to be running on the node) instead of looking it up in the\n434: \t// NodeInfoSnapshot because we don't guarantee that they will be the same.\n435: \t// For example, during preemption, we may pass a copy of the original\n436: \t// nodeInfo object that has some pods removed from it to evaluate the\n437: \t// possibility of preempting them to schedule the target pod.\n438: \tFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\n439: }\n440: \n441: // PostFilterPlugin is an interface for \"PostFilter\" plugins. These plugins are called\n442: // after a pod cannot be scheduled.\n443: type PostFilterPlugin interface {\n444: \tPlugin\n445: \t// PostFilter is called by the scheduling framework\n446: \t// when the scheduling cycle failed at PreFilter or Filter by Unschedulable or UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n447: \t// NodeToStatusMap has statuses that each Node got in the Filter phase.\n448: \t// If this scheduling cycle failed at PreFilter, all Nodes have the status from the rejector PreFilter plugin in NodeToStatusMap.\n449: \t// Note that the scheduling framework runs PostFilter plugins even when PreFilter returned UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n450: \t// In that case, NodeToStatusMap contains all Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n451: \t//\n452: \t// Also, ignoring Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable is the responsibility of each PostFilter plugin,\n453: \t// meaning NodeToStatusMap obviously could have Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\n454: \t// and the scheduling framework does call PostFilter even when all Nodes in NodeToStatusMap are UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n455: \t//\n456: \t// A PostFilter plugin should return one of the following statuses:\n457: \t// - Unschedulable: the plugin gets executed successfully but the pod cannot be made schedulable.\n458: \t// - Success: the plugin gets executed successfully and the pod can be made schedulable.\n459: \t// - Error: the plugin aborts due to some internal error.\n460: \t//\n461: \t// Informational plugins should be configured ahead of other ones, and always return Unschedulable status.\n462: \t// Optionally, a non-nil PostFilterResult may be returned along with a Success status. It must return success and an integer\n495: \t// indicating the rank of the node. Permit\n548: \t// plugins are used to prevent or delay the binding of a Pod. A permit plugin\n549: \t// must return success or wait with timeout duration, or the pod will be rejected.\n550: \t// The pod will also be rejected if the wait timeout or the pod is rejected while\n551: \t// waiting. Each\n561: \t// bind plugin is called in the configured order. A bind plugin may choose whether\n562: \t// or not to handle the given Pod. This structure\n144: // has two sub queues and a additional data structure, namely: activeQ,\n145: // backoffQ and unschedulablePods.\n146: //   - activeQ holds pods that are being considered for scheduling.\n147: //   - backoffQ holds pods that moved from unschedulablePods and will move to\n148: //     activeQ when their backoff periods complete.\n149: //   - unschedulablePods holds pods that were already attempted for scheduling and\n150: //     are currently determined to be unschedulable.\n151: type PriorityQueue struct {\n152: \t*nominator\n153: \n154: \tstop  chan struct{}\n155: \tclock clock.Clock\n156: \n157: \t// pod initial backoff duration.\n158: \tpodInitialBackoffDuration time.Duration\n159: \t// pod maximum backoff duration.\n160: \tpodMaxBackoffDuration time.Duration\n161: \t// the maximum time a pod can stay in the unschedulablePods.\n162: \tpodMaxInUnschedulablePodsDuration time.Duration\n163: \n164: \tcond sync.Cond\n165: \n166: \t// inFlightPods holds the UID of all pods which have been popped out for which Done\n167: \t// hasn't been called yet - in other words, all pods that are currently being\n168: \t// processed (being scheduled, in permit, or in the binding cycle).\n169: \t//\n170: \t// The values in the map are the entry of each pod in the inFlightEvents list.\n171: \t// The value of that entry is the *v1.Pod at the time that scheduling of that\n172: \t// pod started, which can be useful for logging or debugging.\n173: \tinFlightPods map[types.UID]*list.Element\n174: \n175: \t// inFlightEvents holds the events received by the scheduling queue\n176: \t// (entry value is clusterEvent) together with in-flight pods (entry\n177: \t// value is *v1.Pod). Entries get added at the end while the mutex is\n178: \t// locked, so they get serialized.\n179: \t//\n180: \t// The pod entries are added in Pop and used to track which events\n181: \t// occurred after the pod scheduling attempt for that pod started.\n182: \t// They get removed when the scheduling attempt is done, at which\n183: \t// point all events that occurred in the meantime are processed.\n184: \t//\n185: \t// After removal of a pod, events at the start of the list are no\n186: \t// longer needed because all of the other in-flight pods started\n187: \t// later. Those events can be removed.\n188: \tinFlightEvents *list.List\n189: \n190: \t// activeQ is heap structure that scheduler actively looks at to find pods to\n191: \t// schedule. Head of heap is the highest priority pod.\n192: \tactiveQ *heap.Heap\n193: \t// podBackoffQ is a heap ordered by backoff expiry. Pods which have completed backoff\n194: \t// are popped from this heap before the scheduler looks at activeQ\n195: \tpodBackoffQ *heap.Heap\n196: \t// unschedulablePods holds pods that have been tried and determined unschedulable.\n197: \tunschedulablePods *UnschedulablePods\n198: \t// schedulingCycle represents sequence number of scheduling cycle and is incremented\n199: \t// when a pod is popped.\n200: \tschedulingCycle int64\n201: ",

Plugin Framework Initialization\n```\nScheduler.New() [pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go:252]\n  \u251c\u2500 profile.NewMap() [pkg/scheduler/profile/profile.go]\n  \u2502   \u2514\u2500 frameworkruntime.NewFramework() [framework/runtime/framework.go:242]\n  \u2502       \u251c\u2500 Registry.Factory() \u2014 instantiates each plugin\n  \u2502       \u2502   \u2514\u2500 SchedulingQueue.NewSchedulingQueue() [pkg/scheduler/internal/queue/scheduling_queue.go:130]\n      \u2514\u2500 PriorityQueue with activeQ, backoffQ, unschedulablePods\n```\n\n## Design Patterns & Architecture\n\n### Two-Phase Scheduling Design\n\n**Scheduling Cycle (Synchronous Lock Phase)**\n- Pod is popped from queue and sent through filtering/scoring plugins\n- Framework.RunPreFilterPlugins() \u2192 Framework.RunFilterPlugins() \u2192 Framework.RunScorePlugins()\n- Best node is selected\n- **\"Assume\" step**: Pod is marked as running on node in cache (pessimistic locking)\n- Framework.RunReservePluginsReserve() allows plugins to reserve resources\n- Framework.RunPermitPlugins() can delay or reject at last moment\n- Returns CycleState with scheduling decision\n\n**Binding Cycle (Asynchronous Unbind Phase)**\n- Runs in separate goroutine (doesn't block scheduler)\n- Framework.WaitOnPermit() blocks if permit plugins requested wait\n- Framework.RunPreBindPlugins() final checks before binding\n- Framework.RunBindPlugins() creates actual Pod-to-Node binding in API server\n- Framework.RunPostBindPlugins() cleanup/notifications\n- If binding fails, assumed pod is \"forgotten\" from cache, triggering requeue\n\n### Plugin Framework Architecture\n\n**Extension Points (Hooks)**\n1. **PreEnqueue** \u2014 Filter pods before adding to queue (in-place optimization)\n2. **QueueSort** \u2014 Sort pods in scheduling queue (exactly one plugin required)\n3. **PreFilter** \u2014 Pre-process pod; may exclude nodes or skip filter phase\n4. **Filter** \u2014 Run in parallel; determine feasible nodes (replaces old \"Predicates\")\n5. **PostFilter** \u2014 Run if no feasible nodes (e.g., preemption logic)\n6. **PreScore** \u2014 Information-only; ran for feasible nodes\n7. **Score** \u2014 Run in parallel; score each feasible node (replaces old \"Priorities\")\n8. **Reserve** \u2014 Update plugin state after scheduling decision\n9. **Permit** \u2014 Final gate before binding; can wait or reject\n10. **PreBind** \u2014 Final checks immediately before binding\n11. **Bind** \u2014 Perform actual binding (one of plugins in list will bind)\n12. **PostBind** \u2014 Cleanup after successful binding\n\n**Plugin Lifecycle**\n- Plugins are loaded from Registry based on KubeSchedulerProfile configuration\n- Each plugin implements framework.Plugin interface (Name() method)\n- Plugins can optionally implement EnqueueExtensions for event-based requeuing\n- frameworkImpl calls pluginFactoryFunc with context, args, and Handle (which provides access to cache, listers, event recorder)\n- Plugins store scheduling-cycle state in CycleState.storage (thread-safe sync.Map)\n\n### Scheduling Queue\n\n**Three-Queue Model**\n- **activeQ** (priority heap): Pods being actively considered for scheduling\n- **backoffQ** (priority heap by backoff expiry): Pods in backoff after failed attempt\n- **unschedulablePods**: Pods determined unschedulable; moved to backoffQ after timeout\n\n**Queueing Hints & Efficient Requeuing**\n- Plugins implement EnqueueExtensions.EventsToRegister() to specify cluster events they care about\n- When event occurs (e.g., node added, taint removed), only affected pods are requeued\n- Avoids requeuing all pods for every cluster event (performance optimization)\n\n### Cache Architecture\n\n**Assumptions & Snapshot Model**\n- When pod is assumed, it's added to cache with nodeName set\n- Real Pod in API server doesn't have nodeName yet (binding hasn't occurred)\n- Cache maintains assumedPods set and podState map tracking assumed pods and their deadlines\n- Deadlines allow cache to clean up stale assumed pods (prevents memory leaks if binding fails)\n\n**Node Information Management**\n- Cache.NodeInfo tracks pods, resources, and predicates on each node\n- Doubly-linked list of NodeInfo sorted by recency (head = most recent)\n- UpdateSnapshot() called at start of scheduling cycle creates point-in-time view\n- Generation numbers track changes, allowing incremental snapshot updates\n\n**Image States**\n- Tracks image pull latency and availability on nodes\n- Used by plugins like ImageLocality for scheduling decisions\n\n### CycleState Design\n\n**Thread-Safe Scheduling Context**\n- Each pod gets its own CycleState instance for a scheduling cycle\n- Backed by sync.Map for \"write once, read many\" optimization\n- Plugins can store intermediate results (e.g., PreFilter stores computed data read by Filter)\n- Allows zero-copy plugin communication\n\n**State Propagation**\n- PodsToActivateKey reserved key: Plugins can inject pods to be activated post-scheduling\n- SkipFilterPlugins, SkipScorePlugins: PreFilter/PreScore plugins can signal to skip coupled plugins\n- Plugin metrics flags: Controls per-cycle metrics recording\n\n### Multi-Profile Support\n\n**Scheduler Profiles**\n- Scheduler can run multiple scheduler profiles simultaneously\n- Each profile has own Framework, QueueSort, and plugin chain\n- Pods specify .spec.schedulerName to choose profile\n- Allows different scheduling logic for different workload types\n\n## Key Data Structures\n\n### ScheduleResult\n```go\ntype ScheduleResult struct {\n    SuggestedHost string           // Selected node name\n    EvaluatedNodes int             // Nodes evaluated in filtering + beyond\n    FeasibleNodes int              // Nodes that passed filtering\n    nominatingInfo *NominatingInfo // For preemption tracking\n}\n```\n\n### QueuedPodInfo\n```go\ntype QueuedPodInfo struct {\n    Pod                      *v1.Pod\n    Timestamp                time.Time     // When pod entered queue\n    UnschedulablePlugins     sets.Set[string]\n    Attempts                 int           // Scheduling attempts count\n    InitialAttemptTimestamp  *time.Time\n}\n```\n\n### FitError (Scheduling Failure)\n```go\ntype FitError struct {\n    Pod         *v1.Pod\n    NumAllNodes int\n    Diagnosis   Diagnosis\n}\n\ntype Diagnosis struct {\n    NodeToStatusMap map[string]*Status  // Per-node rejection reasons\n    PreFilterMsg    string\n    PostFilterMsg   string\n}\n```\n\n## Data Flow During Scheduling\n\n1. **Pod Arrival**: Pod added to queue via event handler\n2. **Pop Phase**: ScheduleOne pops next pod from queue\n3. **Framework Selection**: Find Framework matching pod's schedulerName\n4. **Snapshot**: Cache.UpdateSnapshot() creates point-in-time node view\n5. **PreFilter**: Plugins may narrow down candidate nodes\n6. **Filter**: Determine feasible nodes (parallel execution)\n7. **Score**: Rank feasible nodes (parallel execution)\n8. **Selection**: Pick best node\n9. **Assume**: Mark pod as running on node in cache\n10. **Reserve**: Plugins update internal state\n11. **Permit**: Final gate; can delay or reject\n12. **Bind (async)**: Wait for permits, run PreBind plugins, call Bind plugins, run PostBind\n13. **Cleanup**: Mark pod as truly scheduled or requeue if binding failed\n\n## Failure Handling\n\n**Scheduling Cycle Failure** \u2192 Handled by FailureHandler\n- PostFilterPlugins run (e.g., preemption to free up resources)\n- Pod moved to backoffQ with exponential backoff\n- Will retry after backoff expires or cluster event occurs\n\n**Binding Cycle Failure** \u2192 Handled by handleBindingCycleError\n- Called if PreBind, Bind, or PostBind plugins fail\n- Reserve plugins' Unreserve methods called to clean up\n- assumed pod forgotten from cache\n- Pod requeued (triggers event-based requeue or backoff)\n\n## Summary\n\nThe Kubernetes scheduler implements a sophisticated two-phase lock-free scheduling architecture using a plugin framework. Pods are sorted via PriorityQueue, processed through a snapshot of cluster state, evaluated by parallel filter/score plugins, and speculatively assumed to run on selected nodes. The binding phase then asynchronously confirms the scheduling decision. The design enables multiple scheduling profiles, efficient event-driven pod requeuing via queueing hints, and extensibility through plugin interfaces at twelve extension points. CycleState provides thread-safe temporary state sharing between plugins, while the cache maintains node information with generation tracking for efficient incremental snapshots. This architecture balances throughput (parallel filtering/scoring), fairness (multiple queue levels with backoff), and extensibility (plugin framework with 12 extension points).\n",

Entry Point: Pod Lifecycle\n```\nEvent Source (API Server)\n  \u2193\neventhandlers.go: addPodToSchedulingQueue()\n  \u2193 (via Informer)\ninternalqueue.SchedulingQueue: Add()\n  \u2193\nPod enters activeQ/backoffQ\n```\n\n### 2. Main Scheduling Loop\n```\nScheduler.Run() [pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go:435]\n  \u2193 (spawns goroutine)\nScheduler.ScheduleOne() [pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go:66]\n  \u2193\nScheduler.NextPod() \u2192 SchedulingQueue.Pop()\n  \u2193 (retrieves next pod from priority queue)\nframework.QueuedPodInfo\n```\n\n### 3. \u251c\u2500 frameworkImpl.runPreFilterPlugin() [runtime/framework.go:700+]\n  \u2502   \u2502   \u2502   \u2502   \u2514\u2500 PreFilterPlugin.PreFilter()\n  \u2502   \u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Scheduler.findNodesThatPassFilters()\n  \u2502   \u2502   \u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Framework.RunFilterPlugins() [runs in parallel via parallelizer]\n  \u2502   \u2502   \u2502   \u2502   \u2502   \u2514\u2500 FilterPlugin.Filter()\n  \u2502   \u2502   \u2502   \u2502   \u2514\u2500 Returns feasibleNodes list\n  \u2502   \u2502   \u2502   \u2514\u2500 Returns diagnosis with node statuses\n  \u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Framework.RunPreScorePlugins()\n  \u2502   \u2502   \u2502   \u2514\u2500 PreScorePlugin.PreScore()\n  \u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500 prioritizeNodes() \u2014 scores via Framework.RunScorePlugins()\n  \u2502   \u2502   \u2502   \u2514\u2500 ScorePlugin.Score() + NormalizeScore()\n  \u2502   \u2502   \u2514\u2500 selectHost() \u2014 picks best node\n  \u2502   \u2502\n  \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Scheduler.assume() \u2014 marks pod as assumed in cache\n  \u2502   \u251c\u2500 Framework.RunReservePluginsReserve() \u2014 reserve plugins update state\n  \u2502   \u2502   \u2514\u2500 ReservePlugin.Reserve()\n  \u2502   \u2514\u2500 Framework.RunPermitPlugins() \u2014 permit plugins can delay/reject\n  \u2502       \u2514\u2500 PermitPlugin.Permit()\n  \u2502\n  \u2514\u2500 Binding Cycle (async via goroutine) [schedule_one.go:118-133]\n      \u2514\u2500 Scheduler.bindingCycle() [schedule_one.go:265]\n          \u251c\u2500 Framework.WaitOnPermit() \u2014 wait for any delayed permits\n          \u251c\u2500 Framework.RunPreBindPlugins()\n          \u2502   \u2514\u2500 PreBindPlugin.PreBind()\n          \u251c\u2500 Scheduler.bind() \u2192 Framework.RunBindPlugins()\n          \u2502   \u2514\u2500 BindPlugin.Bind() \u2014 typically creates pod binding via API\n          \u251c\u2500 Framework.RunPostBindPlugins()\n          \u2502   \u2514\u2500 PostBindPlugin.PostBind()\n          \u2514\u2500 Cache.ForgetPod() OR Cache.AssumedPods cleanup\n```\n\n### 4. Plugin Framework Initialization\n```\nScheduler.New() [pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go:252]\n  \u251c\u2500 profile.NewMap() [pkg/scheduler/profile/profile.go]\n  \u2502   \u2514\u2500 frameworkruntime.NewFramework() [framework/runtime/framework.go:242]\n  \u2502       \u251c\u2500 Registry.Factory() \u2014 instantiates each plugin\n  \u2502       \u2502   \u2514\u2500 pluginFactoryFunc(ctx, args, handle)\n  \u2502       \u251c\u2500 frameworkImpl.getExtensionPoints()\n  \u2502       \u251c\u2500 updatePluginList() \u2014 assigns plugins to extension point lists\n  \u2502       \u251c\u2500 frameworkImpl.expandMultiPointPlugins()\n  \u2502       \u2514\u2500 frameworkImpl.setInstrumentedPlugins() \u2014 wraps with metrics\n  \u2502\n  \u2514\u2500 SchedulingQueue.NewSchedulingQueue() [pkg/scheduler/internal/queue/scheduling_queue.go:130]\n      \u2514\u2500 PriorityQueue with activeQ, backoffQ, unschedulablePods\n```\n\n## Design Patterns & Architecture\n\n### Two-Phase Scheduling Design\n\n**Scheduling Cycle (Synchronous Lock Phase)**\n- Pod is popped from queue and sent through filtering/scoring plugins\n- Framework.RunPreFilterPlugins() \u2192 Framework.RunFilterPlugins() \u2192 Framework.RunScorePlugins()\n- Best node is selected\n- **\"Assume\" step**: Pod is marked as running on node in cache (pessimistic locking)\n- Framework.RunReservePluginsReserve() allows plugins to reserve resources\n- Framework.RunPermitPlugins() can delay or reject at last moment\n- Returns CycleState with scheduling decision\n\n**Binding Cycle (Asynchronous Unbind Phase)**\n- Runs in separate goroutine (doesn't block scheduler)\n- Framework.WaitOnPermit() blocks if permit plugins requested wait\n- Framework.RunPreBindPlugins() final checks before binding\n- Framework.RunBindPlugins() creates actual Pod-to-Node binding in API server\n- Framework.RunPostBindPlugins() cleanup/notifications\n- If binding fails, assumed pod is \"forgotten\" from cache, triggering requeue\n\n### Plugin Framework Architecture\n\n**Extension Points (Hooks)**\n1. **PreEnqueue** \u2014 Filter pods before adding to queue (in-place optimization)\n2. **QueueSort** \u2014 Sort pods in scheduling queue (exactly one plugin required)\n3. **PreFilter** \u2014 Pre-process pod; may exclude nodes or skip filter phase\n4. **Filter** \u2014 Run in parallel; determine feasible nodes (replaces old \"Predicates\")\n5. **PostFilter** \u2014 Run if no feasible nodes (e.g., preemption logic)\n6. **PreScore** \u2014 Information-only; ran for feasible nodes\n7. **Score** \u2014 Run in parallel; score each feasible node (replaces old \"Priorities\")\n8. **Reserve** \u2014 Update plugin state after scheduling decision\n9. **Permit** \u2014 Final gate before binding; can wait or reject\n10. **PreBind** \u2014 Final checks immediately before binding\n11. **Bind** \u2014 Perform actual binding (one of plugins in list will bind)\n12. **PostBind** \u2014 Cleanup after successful binding\n\n**Plugin Lifecycle**\n- Plugins are loaded from Registry based on KubeSchedulerProfile configuration\n- Each plugin implements framework.Plugin interface (Name() method)\n- Plugins can optionally implement EnqueueExtensions for event-based requeuing\n- frameworkImpl calls pluginFactoryFunc with context, args, and Handle (which provides access to cache, listers, event recorder)\n- Plugins store scheduling-cycle state in CycleState.storage (thread-safe sync.Map)\n\n### Scheduling Queue\n\n**Three-Queue Model**\n- **activeQ** (priority heap): Pods being actively considered for scheduling\n- **backoffQ** (priority heap by backoff expiry): Pods in backoff after failed attempt\n- **unschedulablePods**: Pods determined unschedulable; moved to backoffQ after timeout\n\n**Queueing Hints & Efficient Requeuing**\n- Plugins implement EnqueueExtensions.EventsToRegister() to specify cluster events they care about\n- When event occurs (e.g., node added, taint removed), only affected pods are requeued\n- Avoids requeuing all pods for every cluster event (performance optimization)\n\n### Cache Architecture\n\n**Assumptions & Snapshot Model**\n- When pod is assumed, it's added to cache with nodeName set\n- Real Pod in API server doesn't have nodeName yet (binding hasn't occurred)\n- Cache maintains assumedPods set and podState map tracking assumed pods and their deadlines\n- Deadlines allow cache to clean up stale assumed pods (prevents memory leaks if binding fails)\n\n**Node Information Management**\n- Cache.NodeInfo tracks pods, resources, and predicates on each node\n- Doubly-linked list of NodeInfo sorted by recency (head = most recent)\n- UpdateSnapshot() called at start of scheduling cycle creates point-in-time view\n- Generation numbers track changes, allowing incremental snapshot updates\n\n**Image States**\n- Tracks image pull latency and availability on nodes\n- Used by plugins like ImageLocality for scheduling decisions\n\n### CycleState Design\n\n**Thread-Safe Scheduling Context**\n- Each pod gets its own CycleState instance for a scheduling cycle\n- Backed by sync.Map for \"write once, read many\" optimization\n- Plugins can store intermediate results (e.g., PreFilter stores computed data read by Filter)\n- Allows zero-copy plugin communication\n\n**State Propagation**\n- PodsToActivateKey reserved key: Plugins can inject pods to be activated post-scheduling\n- SkipFilterPlugins, SkipScorePlugins: PreFilter/PreScore plugins can signal to skip coupled plugins\n- Plugin metrics flags: Controls per-cycle metrics recording\n\n### Multi-Profile Support\n\n**Scheduler Profiles**\n- Scheduler can run multiple scheduler profiles simultaneously\n- Each profile has own Framework, QueueSort, and plugin chain\n- Pods specify .spec.schedulerName to choose profile\n- Allows different scheduling logic for different workload types\n\n## Key Data Structures\n\n### ScheduleResult\n```go\ntype ScheduleResult struct {\n    SuggestedHost string           // Selected node name\n    EvaluatedNodes int             // Nodes evaluated in filtering + beyond\n    FeasibleNodes int              // Nodes that passed filtering\n    nominatingInfo *NominatingInfo // For preemption tracking\n}\n```\n\n### QueuedPodInfo\n```go\ntype QueuedPodInfo struct {\n    Pod                      *v1.Pod\n    Timestamp                time.Time     // When pod entered queue\n    UnschedulablePlugins     sets.Set[string]\n    Attempts                 int           // Scheduling attempts count\n    InitialAttemptTimestamp  *time.Time\n}\n```\n\n### FitError (Scheduling Failure)\n```go\ntype FitError struct {\n    Pod         *v1.Pod\n    NumAllNodes int\n    Diagnosis   Diagnosis\n}\n\ntype Diagnosis struct {\n    NodeToStatusMap map[string]*Status  // Per-node rejection reasons\n    PreFilterMsg    string\n    PostFilterMsg   string\n}\n```\n\n## Data Flow During Scheduling\n\n1. **Pod Arrival**: Pod added to queue via event handler\n2. **Pop Phase**: ScheduleOne pops next pod from queue\n3. **Framework Selection**: Find Framework matching pod's schedulerName\n4. **Snapshot**: Cache.UpdateSnapshot() creates point-in-time node view\n5. **PreFilter**: Plugins may narrow down candidate nodes\n6. **Filter**: Determine feasible nodes (parallel execution)\n7. **Score**: Rank feasible nodes (parallel execution)\n8. **Selection**: Pick best node\n9. **Assume**: Mark pod as running on node in cache\n10. **Reserve**: Plugins update internal state\n11. **Permit**: Final gate; can delay or reject\n12. **Bind (async)**: Wait for permits, run PreBind plugins, call Bind plugins, run PostBind\n13. **Cleanup**: Mark pod as truly scheduled or requeue if binding failed\n\n## Failure Handling\n\n**Scheduling Cycle Failure** \u2192 Handled by FailureHandler\n- PostFilterPlugins run (e.g., preemption to free up resources)\n- Pod moved to backoffQ with exponential backoff\n- Will retry after backoff expires or cluster event occurs\n\n**Binding Cycle Failure** \u2192 Handled by handleBindingCycleError\n- Called if PreBind, Bind, or PostBind plugins fail\n- Reserve plugins' Unreserve methods called to clean up\n- assumed pod forgotten from cache\n- Pod requeued (triggers event-based requeue or backoff)\n\n## Summary\n\nThe Kubernetes scheduler implements a sophisticated two-phase lock-free scheduling architecture using a plugin framework. Pods are sorted via PriorityQueue, processed through a snapshot of cluster state, evaluated by parallel filter/score plugins, and speculatively assumed to run on selected nodes. The binding phase then asynchronously confirms the scheduling decision. The design enables multiple scheduling profiles, efficient event-driven pod requeuing via queueing hints, and extensibility through plugin interfaces at twelve extension points. CycleState provides thread-safe temporary state sharing between plugins, while the cache maintains node information with generation tracking for efficient incremental snapshots. This architecture balances throughput (parallel filtering/scoring), fairness (multiple queue levels with backoff), and extensibility (plugin framework with 12 extension points).\n",

# Kubernetes Scheduler Architecture Analysis

## Files Examined

### Core Scheduler
- **pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go** — Main Scheduler struct managing lifecycle, initialization of queue/cache/profiles, and the main Run loop
- **pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go** — Contains ScheduleOne entry point and the two-phase scheduling/binding cycle implementation
- **pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go** — Event handlers that watch cluster events and feed pods into the scheduling queue

### Framework & Plugin System
- **pkg/scheduler/framework/interface.go** — Defines all plugin interfaces (PreFilter, Filter, Score, Reserve, Permit, Bind, etc.), Framework interface, and Status codes
- **pkg/scheduler/framework/cycle_state.go** — CycleState struct for sharing data between plugins within a scheduling cycle
- **pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/framework.go** — frameworkImpl implementing the Framework interface; instantiates plugins and executes them
- **pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/registry.go** — Plugin registry mapping plugin names to factory functions
- **pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/** — Built-in plugin implementations (NodeResourcesFit, InterPodAffinity, PodTopologySpread, etc.)

### Scheduling Queue
- **pkg/scheduler/internal/queue/scheduling_queue.go** — SchedulingQueue interface and PriorityQueue implementation with activeQ, backoffQ, unschedulablePods sub-queues
- **pkg/scheduler/internal/queue/events.go** — Cluster events and queueing hints for requeuing pods

### Cache
- **pkg/scheduler/internal/cache/cache.go** — Cache struct managing assumed pods, node info, and image states
- **pkg/scheduler/internal/cache/snapshot.go** — Snapshot of cache taken at start of scheduling cycle
- **pkg/scheduler/internal/cache/node_tree.go** — Efficient node lookup structure
